          UTC-4
         </a>
         )
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA,_2012.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2943" data-file-width="2256" height="457" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg/350px-Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg/525px-Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg/700px-Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA%2C_2012.jpg 2x" width="350"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Washington-Baltimore-Arlington_CSA,_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the current
         <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
          OMB
         </a>
         -designated Washington-Baltimore-Arlington, DC-MD-VA-WV-PA Combined Statistical Area.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area
       </b>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       consisting of the overlapping labor market region of the cities of
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington, D.C.
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">
        Baltimore, Maryland
       </a>
       . The region includes Central
       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">
        Maryland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Virginia" title="Northern Virginia">
        Northern Virginia
       </a>
       , three counties in the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle_of_West_Virginia" title="Eastern Panhandle of West Virginia">
        Eastern Panhandle of West Virginia
       </a>
       , and one county in
       <a href="/wiki/South_Central_Pennsylvania" title="South Central Pennsylvania">
        South Central Pennsylvania
       </a>
       . It is the most educated, highest-income, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Table_of_United_States_Combined_Statistical_Areas" title="Table of United States Combined Statistical Areas">
        fourth largest
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">
        combined statistical area
       </a>
       in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Officially, the area is designated by the
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">
        Office of Management and Budget
       </a>
       (OMB) as the
       <b>
        Washington–Baltimore–Arlington, DC–MD–VA–WV–PA Combined Statistical Area
       </b>
       . It is composed primarily of two major
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">
        metropolitan statistical areas
       </a>
       (MSA), the
       <a href="/wiki/Washington_metropolitan_area" title="Washington metropolitan area">
        Washington–Arlington–Alexandria, DC–VA–MD–WV
       </a>
       MSA and the
       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_metropolitan_area" title="Baltimore metropolitan area">
        Baltimore–Columbia–Towson, MD
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" title="Metropolitan Statistical Area">
        MSA
       </a>
       . In addition, six other smaller urban areas not contiguous to the main urban area but having strong commuting ties with the main area are also included in the metropolitan area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These are: the
       <a href="/wiki/Hagerstown_metropolitan_area" title="Hagerstown metropolitan area">
        Hagerstown–Martinsburg, MD–WV
       </a>
       MSA, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franklin_County,_PA" title="Franklin County, PA">
        Chambersburg–Waynesboro, PA
       </a>
       MSA, the
       <a href="/wiki/Winchester,_VA%E2%80%93WV_MSA" title="Winchester, VA–WV MSA">
        Winchester, VA–WV
       </a>
       MSA, the
       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_County,_Maryland" title="St. Mary's County, Maryland">
        California–Lexington Park, MD
       </a>
       MSA, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Talbot_County,_MD" title="Talbot County, MD">
        Easton, MD
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">
        micropolitan statistical area
       </a>
       (µSA), and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorchester_County,_MD" title="Dorchester County, MD">
        Cambridge, MD
       </a>
       µSA.
      </p>
      <p>
       Some counties such as
       <a href="/wiki/Caroline_County,_Virginia" title="Caroline County, Virginia">
        Caroline
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/King_George_County,_Virginia" title="King George County, Virginia">
        King George County
       </a>
       , Virginia are not officially designated by the OMB as members of this metropolitan area, but still consider themselves members anyway.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is mostly due to their proximity to the area, the size of their commuter population, and by the influence of local broadcasting stations. The population of the entire Washington-Baltimore Combined Statistical Area as of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Census_Bureau" title="US Census Bureau">
        Census Bureau's
       </a>
       2012
       <a href="/wiki/Population_Estimates_Program" title="Population Estimates Program">
        Population Estimates
       </a>
       is 9,331,587.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most populous city is Washington, DC, with a population of 681,170.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most populous county is
       <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_County,_Virginia" title="Fairfax County, Virginia">
        Fairfax County, Virginia
       </a>
       , with a population exceeding 1.1 million.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Components_of_the_metropolitan_area">
        Components of the metropolitan area
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </a>

        </span>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_organizations">
        Regional organizations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Regional organizations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_Washington_Council_of_Governments">
        Metropolitan Washington Council of Governments
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Metropolitan Washington Council of Governments">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Founded in 1957, the
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Washington_Council_of_Governments" title="Metropolitan Washington Council of Governments">
        Metropolitan Washington Council of Governments
       </a>
       (MWCOG) is a regional organization of 23 Washington-area local governments, as well as area members of the
       <a href="/wiki/Maryland_General_Assembly" title="Maryland General Assembly">
        Maryland
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">
        Virginia
       </a>
       state legislatures, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Senate" title="U.S. Senate">
        U.S. Senate
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House_of_Representatives" title="U.S. House of Representatives">
        U.S. House of Representatives
       </a>
       . MWCOG provides a forum for discussion and the development of regional responses to issues regarding the environment, transportation, public safety, homeland security, affordable housing, community planning, and economic development.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Capital_Region_Transportation_Planning_Board&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Capital Region Transportation Planning Board (page does not exist)">
        National Capital Region Transportation Planning Board
       </a>
       , a component of MWCOG, is the federally designated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Planning_Organization" title="Metropolitan Planning Organization">
        Metropolitan Planning Organization
       </a>
       for the metropolitan Washington area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Baltimore_Metropolitan_Council">
        Baltimore Metropolitan Council
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Baltimore Metropolitan Council">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The Baltimore Metropolitan Council is the equivalent organization for the Baltimore portion of the combined Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The BMC, which was created in 1992 as the successor to the Regional Planning Council and Baltimore Regional Council of Governments, consists of the Baltimore region's elected executives, representing Baltimore City and Anne Arundel, Baltimore, Carroll, Harford and Howard counties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baltometro.org_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-baltometro.org-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore_Regional_Transportation_Board&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Baltimore Regional Transportation Board (page does not exist)">
        Baltimore Regional Transportation Board
       </a>
       is the federally recognized Metropolitan Planning Organization for transportation planning in the Baltimore region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baltometro.org_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-baltometro.org-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_principal_cities">
        List of principal cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: List of principal cities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        See
        <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area" title="List of cities in the Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area">
         List of cities in the Baltimore–Washington metropolitan area
        </a>
        for a full list.
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Primary_industries">
        Primary industries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Primary industries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Biotechnology">
        Biotechnology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Biotechnology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Not limited to its proximity to the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Institutes_of_Health" title="National Institutes of Health">
        National Institutes of Health
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Bethesda,_Maryland" title="Bethesda, Maryland">
        Bethesda
       </a>
       , Maryland's Washington suburbs are a major center for
       <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
        biotechnology
       </a>
       . Prominent local biotechnology companies include
       <a href="/wiki/MedImmune" title="MedImmune">
        MedImmune
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/United_Therapeutics" title="United Therapeutics">
        United Therapeutics
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Institute_for_Genomic_Research" title="The Institute for Genomic Research">
        The Institute for Genomic Research
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Genome_Sciences" title="Human Genome Sciences">
        Human Genome Sciences
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes_Medical_Institute" title="Howard Hughes Medical Institute">
        Howard Hughes Medical Institute
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Defense_contracting">
        Defense contracting
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Defense contracting">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Many defense contractors are based in Northern Virginia and Montgomery County, Maryland to be close to
       <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">
        the Pentagon
       </a>
       in Arlington. Local defense contractors include
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin" title="Lockheed Martin">
        Lockheed Martin
       </a>
       , the largest, as well as
       <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Grumman" title="Northrop Grumman">
        Northrop Grumman
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/General_Dynamics" title="General Dynamics">
        General Dynamics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems_Inc." title="BAE Systems Inc.">
        BAE Systems Inc.
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_Sciences_Corporation" title="Computer Sciences Corporation">
        Computer Sciences Corporation
       </a>
       (CSC),
       <a href="/wiki/Booz_Allen_Hamilton" title="Booz Allen Hamilton">
        Booz Allen Hamilton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Leidos" title="Leidos">
        Leidos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Science_Applications_International_Corporation" title="Science Applications International Corporation">
        Science Applications International Corporation
       </a>
       (SAIC), and
       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences_Corporation" title="Orbital Sciences Corporation">
        Orbital Sciences Corporation
       </a>
       .
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_airports">
        Major airports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Major airports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_International_Thurgood_Marshall_Airport" title="Baltimore–Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport">
         Baltimore–Washington International Thurgood Marshall Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Anne_Arundel_County,_Maryland" title="Anne Arundel County, Maryland">
         Anne Arundel County, Maryland
        </a>
        – closest to Baltimore and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_States_by_passengers_boarded" title="List of airports in the United States by passengers boarded">
         busiest in region
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
         <a href="#cite_note-24">
          [24]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_Washington_National_Airport" title="Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport">
         Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia" title="Arlington County, Virginia">
         Arlington County, Virginia
        </a>
        – closest to Washington.)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Washington_Dulles_International_Airport" title="Washington Dulles International Airport">
         Washington Dulles International Airport
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Chantilly,_Virginia" title="Chantilly, Virginia">
         Chantilly, Virginia
        </a>
        – the region's main international airport.)
       </li>
      </ul>

            <span class="reference-accessdate">
             . Retrieved
             <span class="nowrap">
              16 November
             </span>
             2017
            </span>
            .
           </cite>
           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=Forbes.com&amp;rft.atitle=Whiting-Turner+Contracting+on+the+Forbes+America%27s+Largest+Private+Companies+List&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.forbes.com%2Fcompanies%2Fwhiting-turner-contracting%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABaltimore%E2%80%93Washington+metropolitan+area">
            <span style="display:none;">
            </span>
           </span>
          </span>
         </li>
         <li id="cite_note-24">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-24">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           As according to
           <a class="external text" href="http://www.faa.gov/airports/planning_capacity/passenger_allcargo_stats/passenger/media/prelim_cy11_primary_enplanements.pdf" rel="nofollow">
            Federal Aviation Administration CY 2011 Enplanement Data
           </a>
           <sup class="noprint Inline-Template">
            <span style="white-space: nowrap;">
             [
             <i>
              <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot">
               <span title=" Dead link since November 2016">
                permanent dead link
               </span>
              </a>
             </i>
             ]
            </span>
           </sup>
           , BWI exceeded Dulles by less than 24,000 passengers. As of 2010
           <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Baltimore%E2%80%93Washington_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit">
             [update]
            </a>
           </sup>
           , however, Dulles has an edge in international traffic.
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>

        <tr>
         <td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" colspan="2" style="width:100%;padding:0px">
          <div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
           The District of Columbia itself, and
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Independent_city_(Virginia)" title="Independent city (Virginia)">
            Virginia's incorporated cities
           </a>
           , are
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/County-equivalent" title="County-equivalent">
            county equivalents
           </a>
           . Virginia's incorporated cities are listed under their surrounding county. The incorporated cities bordering more than one county (
           <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">
            Alexandria
           </a>
           ,
           <a href="/wiki/Falls_Church,_Virginia" title="Falls Church, Virginia">
            Falls Church
           </a>
           and
           <a href="/wiki/Fredericksburg,_Virginia" title="Fredericksburg, Virginia">
            Fredericksburg
           </a>
           ) are listed under the county they were part of before incorporation as a city.
          </div>
         </td>
